Accounting Software
Module Reference Guide
Detailed overview of each module — purpose, functionality, and required data fields
CUSTOMER ACCOUNTS
1. Customer Data
Customer Data is the master record that stores all essential information about each customer. It serves as the foundation for all customer-related transactions throughout the software.
Purpose: To maintain a centralised database of all customers, enabling quick access during invoicing, quotations, and payment tracking.

2. Quotation Preparation
Quotation Preparation allows the business to create formal price offers for potential or existing customers before a sale is confirmed. It is a pre-sales document.
Purpose: To provide customers with a formal offer outlining the goods or services, quantities, and prices — which can later be converted into a sales invoice.

3. Sales Invoice
A Sales Invoice is the primary document raised by the business to bill a customer for goods sold or services rendered. It is a legally binding document and forms the basis for accounts receivable and GST reporting.
Purpose: To record revenue, create a receivable entry in the customer's account, and generate data for GST returns (GSTR-1).

4. Debit Note (Customer)
A Debit Note raised on a customer is used to increase the amount owed by the customer. It is typically issued when additional charges need to be billed after the original invoice.
Purpose: To revise an earlier invoice upwards — for instance, to charge for additional freight, price corrections, or extra services not included in the original invoice.

5. Credit Note (Customer)
A Credit Note issued to a customer reduces the amount owed by the customer. It is raised when goods are returned, when there is a billing error, or when a discount is given after invoicing.
Purpose: To reverse or reduce a previously raised sales invoice — either partially or fully. It also adjusts GST liability in GSTR-1.

VENDOR ACCOUNTS
1. Vendor Data
Vendor Data is the master record for all suppliers from whom goods or services are procured. It is the equivalent of Customer Data on the purchase side.
Purpose: To maintain a complete and accurate database of all vendors, enabling efficient purchase processing, payment tracking, and reconciliation.

2. Vendor Invoice
A Vendor Invoice (also called a Purchase Invoice) is raised when goods or services are received from a vendor and the vendor's bill is entered into the system. It creates a payable entry in the vendor's account.
Purpose: To record purchases, account for Input Tax Credit (ITC) on GST paid, and track amounts payable to vendors. It feeds into GSTR-2B reconciliation.

3. Debit Note (Vendor)
A Debit Note raised on a vendor is issued by your business to the vendor, indicating that you are reducing the amount payable to them. This typically happens when goods are returned or when you find an overcharge.
Purpose: To reverse or reduce a vendor invoice — such as in the case of purchase returns, quality rejections, or price corrections. Also reverses the ITC claimed.

4. Recurring Expense
Recurring Expense is a feature that allows the system to automatically create vendor invoices or expense entries on a defined schedule for expenses that occur regularly.
Purpose: To automate the entry of fixed periodic expenses such as rent, subscriptions, retainers, AMC charges, and utility bills — reducing manual effort and ensuring no expense is missed.

BANKING
1. Bank
The Bank module manages all transactions related to bank accounts — including receipts from customers, payments to vendors, bank charges, interest credits, and inter-bank transfers.
Purpose: To record all bank transactions, maintain an accurate bank ledger, and facilitate bank reconciliation by matching system entries with bank statements.

2. Cash
The Cash module records all transactions involving physical cash — petty cash expenses, cash sales, cash receipts, and cash payments. It maintains the cash book of the business.
Purpose: To track day-to-day cash movements accurately, maintain a running cash balance, and ensure proper accountability of petty cash and cash-in-hand.

ACCOUNTANT
1. Manual Journal
A Manual Journal (or Journal Voucher) is used to record accounting entries that do not arise from standard sales, purchases, or banking transactions. It gives the accountant direct control over the general ledger.
Purpose: To pass adjustment entries, rectification entries, depreciation, provisions, accruals, prepayments, and any other entries that require direct debit/credit posting to ledger accounts.

2. Recurring Journal
Recurring Journal automates the creation of periodic journal entries that need to be posted on a regular schedule — similar to Recurring Expenses but for general ledger adjustments.
Purpose: To automate entries like monthly depreciation, prepaid expense amortisation, accrued income recognition, and interest calculations without manual intervention each period.

OTHERS
1. Transaction Locking
Transaction Locking is a control feature that prevents modification or deletion of accounting entries after a specified date. It protects the integrity of completed and audited periods.
Purpose: To lock closed accounting periods (monthly, quarterly, or annual) so that no accidental or unauthorised changes can be made to finalised transactions.

2. Chart of Accounts
The Chart of Accounts (COA) is the complete list of all ledger accounts used in the accounting system. It is the backbone of the entire accounting structure.
Purpose: To organise and classify all financial transactions into appropriate accounts — enabling accurate financial reporting, trial balance, and statutory compliance.

3. Fixed Asset Register
The Fixed Asset Register maintains a record of all long-term tangible assets owned by the business — such as machinery, vehicles, furniture, computers, and buildings.
Purpose: To track the acquisition, depreciation, disposal, and current book value of all fixed assets, and to ensure compliance with accounting standards and income tax regulations.

4. Partners Account
Partners Account tracks the capital contributions, drawings, profit sharing, and current accounts of partners in a partnership or LLP firm.
Purpose: To maintain separate ledgers for each partner — recording their capital introduced, drawings taken, interest on capital, salary/commission due, and share of profits and losses.

Job Register
The Job Register is used to track income and expenses against specific jobs, projects, contracts, or assignments. It enables project-wise profitability analysis.
Purpose: To monitor the financial performance of individual jobs or projects by linking all related revenues and costs to a job code — useful for contractors, service firms, and project-based businesses.

REPORTS
1. Profit and Loss Account
The Profit and Loss (P&L) Account summarises all income and expenses over a defined period to show the net profit or net loss of the business.
Key Fields: Date range, income heads (sales, other income), direct and indirect expense heads, gross profit, operating profit, and net profit/loss.
2. Balance Sheet
The Balance Sheet presents the financial position of the business at a specific point in time, showing assets, liabilities, and equity/capital.
Key Fields: As-at date, fixed and current assets, current and long-term liabilities, capital accounts, reserves and surplus, and net worth.
3. Trial Balance
The Trial Balance lists all ledger accounts with their debit and credit balances to verify that the books are arithmetically balanced.
Key Fields: Date range, account code, account name, opening balance, transactions during the period, and closing balance in debit/credit columns.
4. Cash Flow Statement
The Cash Flow Statement shows how cash moves in and out of the business across operating, investing, and financing activities over a period.
Key Fields: Period, operating activities (receipts and payments), investing activities (asset purchases/sales), financing activities (loans, capital), and net change in cash.
5. AR Ageing Summary
The Accounts Receivable Ageing Summary categorises outstanding customer dues by how long they have been overdue.
Key Fields: Customer name, invoice number and date, total outstanding, and buckets such as 0-30 days, 31-60 days, 61-90 days, and 90+ days overdue.
6. AP Ageing Summary
The Accounts Payable Ageing Summary categorises outstanding vendor payables by overdue period.
Key Fields: Vendor name, invoice reference, total payable, and ageing buckets (0-30, 31-60, 61-90, 90+ days) to identify urgent payments.
7. Sales Register
The Sales Register lists all sales invoices raised during a period with full details — used for sales analysis and GSTR-1 preparation.
Key Fields: Invoice number and date, customer name, GSTIN, place of supply, taxable value, GST breakup (CGST/SGST/IGST), and total invoice value.
8. Debit Note Register (Customer)
Lists all debit notes raised on customers during a period — tracks additional charges billed and their GST implications.
Key Fields: Debit note number and date, customer name, original invoice reference, reason, taxable value, GST amount, and net debit amount.
9. Credit Note Register (Customer)
Lists all credit notes issued to customers — used to track returns, discounts, and billing reversals, and to report in GSTR-1.
Key Fields: Credit note number and date, customer name, original invoice reference, reason for credit, taxable value, GST reversal, and net credit amount.
10. Purchase Register
The Purchase Register lists all vendor invoices recorded during a period — forms the basis for ITC claims and vendor analysis.
Key Fields: Vendor invoice number and date, vendor name and GSTIN, item description, HSN/SAC, taxable value, CGST/SGST/IGST, and total invoice value.
11. Debit Note (Vendor) Register
Lists all debit notes raised on vendors (purchase return notes) — tracks ITC reversals and returns to suppliers.
Key Fields: Debit note number and date, vendor name, original purchase invoice, goods returned, taxable value, GST reversed, and net debit to vendor.
12. GSTR-1 Summary
GSTR-1 is the monthly or quarterly outward supply return filed by GST-registered businesses. This report compiles all sales data in the prescribed format.
Key Fields: B2B invoices (with customer GSTIN), B2C invoices, exports, credit/debit notes, nil-rated and exempt supplies, HSN-wise summary, and consolidated tax liability.
13. GSTR-2B Summary
GSTR-2B is the auto-drafted input tax credit statement generated from supplier filings. This report shows ITC available for claiming.
Key Fields: Vendor GSTIN, invoice details, ITC available (CGST/SGST/IGST), ITC ineligible under Section 17(5), and reconciliation status with purchase register.
14. GSTR Summary
A consolidated GST summary report giving an overview of total output tax liability and input tax credit across all GST returns for the period.
Key Fields: Total output GST (from GSTR-1), total ITC (from GSTR-2B), net GST payable, and period-wise comparison.
15. Ledger Statement
A Ledger Statement shows all debit and credit entries for a specific ledger account during a selected period, with running balance.
Key Fields: Account name, date range, opening balance, date-wise transactions with narration and voucher reference, and closing balance.
16. Job Register
The Job Register report lists all jobs with their financial summary — revenues, costs, and profitability.
Key Fields: Job code and name, customer, start and end dates, contract value, total expenses, invoices raised, and gross profit/loss per job.
17. Job Wise Profit Report
Provides a detailed profitability analysis for each job — breaking down income and expenditure to compute gross and net profit at the job level.
Key Fields: Job code, income billed, cost breakdown by category (materials, labour, subcontract, overheads), gross profit, and profit margin percentage.
18. Sales by Customer
Analyses total sales made to each customer during a period — useful for identifying top customers and tracking buying patterns.
Key Fields: Customer name, number of invoices, total taxable value, total GST, total invoice value, and percentage contribution to overall sales.
19. Sales by Charges
Breaks down sales by individual income heads or service charges — showing which products or services contribute most to revenue.
Key Fields: Charge/item description, HSN/SAC code, total quantity sold, total taxable value, and GST for each charge or product category.
20. Purchase by Vendor
Summarises total purchases from each vendor over a period — used for vendor analysis, negotiation, and spend management.
Key Fields: Vendor name, number of invoices, total taxable purchases, ITC claimed, total purchase value, and vendor's share of total purchases.
21. Purchase by Charges
Breaks down purchases by expense head or item category — showing where the business is spending its procurement budget.
Key Fields: Expense head, item description, HSN/SAC, total quantity purchased, taxable value, ITC amount, and total expenditure per category.
22. Day Book
The Day Book (also called the Daily Transaction Report) lists all transactions entered in the system on a given date — across all modules.
Key Fields: Date, voucher number, voucher type (sales, purchase, receipt, payment, journal), party name, amount, and account heads involved.
23. Journal Report
The Journal Report lists all manual journal entries passed during a selected period — useful for review and audit.
Key Fields: Journal number and date, debit and credit accounts, amounts, narration, and the name of the user who created and approved the entry.
24. Ledger Statement
(Duplicate listing in report menu — same as report No. 15 above.) The Ledger Statement gives a full account history for any selected ledger account over a chosen date range.
Key Fields: Account name, period selected, opening balance, chronological list of all transactions with dates, voucher references, narrations, debit and credit amounts, and closing balance.
